et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 And ensure that you do not press into the gap, and move your hand all along the bone up to the end, without touching it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	 And if there is swelling at the beginning of the gap, gently push into the gap slightly until it appears.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 Then remove as we have said, then wet cloths for ease and cooling, place it on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if there are such men who crush stones and place them there to destroy that moisture which has been lodged there.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then the healer works until it is sound again.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess comes to heat at that place, then the healer treats with plasters until it is sound again.
des poilz des papieres	Of hair from parchment papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	 When hairs grow other than naturally and become old, they harm the eyes, causing diseases as tears are accustomed to and softening of the skin and pus formation, until it is due to the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	 And there are four methods of treatment:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 Or by fire and lancet together according to what precedes or the chapter on cautery, and it is done either through incision and suturing or with bandages, as I will describe.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	 It is necessary to place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of oil into your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	 if it flows well, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	 if not, let her pour an arrow through all the thread at once;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	 and be it near the edge of the paper or hairs sprout from there among these hairs, then draw the thread through all over the paper and turn it to smooth.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	 then cut into the area below the paper, away from the hairs closest to it, covering all the shining part from the large to the small notch.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 First remove the thread and place a small tent of cotton or linen underneath the paper, then press down on the paper with a mold similar to a lime bell, so that it should also be according to the quantity you see rising in the paper which is visible at all times.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	 And if there is a part that requires cutting off a great quantity of paper according to how the paper becomes moistened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	 then make all the fatty tissue beneath the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large ridge up to small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	 and let there be a division near the natural hair growth at the root of the swelling, then insert the needle into one of the two corners as seen, then scrape it all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	 Then join the two lips with a stitch from a needle using one thread of fine wool yarn, and bleed the blood, and trim any excess threads around both eyebrows as you do so.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	 And if not, then pay it no heed, leave the stitch and threads until three or four days have passed.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	 Then treat the wound without removing any dried or tightened stitching materials, as the paper will loosen with the pressure of the wound and healing, but the stitches are movable (as say the ancients), which requires careful work.
et si a une autre maniere:	 And if by another method:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 It is that you shape the paper as if it were like the skirt of a rosemary bush, as we have described, removing three or four lines every three days according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then follow those who ascend with small, evenly matched strengths according to the form here shown.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	 If you cannot hold the tongs, and things are not equal, take a needle or wire of any kind, and place it in the wound.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	 And thread another line up to the great gash, and a second line down to the small one, and join together between the two lines evenly.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then lift your hand evenly, and raise all the skin over which you have marked, as we have described, then stitch together both edges of the wound with sutures, until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	 And if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerotype and similar soothing ointment.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	 And sometimes the hair of the skin is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	 If it is necessary to use what we have said about making an incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 However, the suture on either side is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	 The treatment of abscesses should be as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	 and that you convert the paper and stretch it out thinly as I have instructed, then make abscesses by skillful technique, with fine ligatures as long as the paper and the width of the gauze.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	 and bind as two sides where you hold the threads.
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	 then carefully join the top part to that of the oil paper, and tie the two abscesses with fine ligatures.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 and leave it thus for several days, and the skin that has been stretched will wither, dry up, and shrink until it tightens on its own.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 If it delays, if the cap is affected by forces, then treat until it becomes whole again.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	 And when the wound heals quickly, and if there are no more papery edges, and hair cannot grow anymore.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 This is the form of two sticks that you will make according to this shape, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	 The techniques are such that you should use a fine needle, and wind silk thread delicate and subtle.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	 Then connect the heads and carefully wrap one around the other subtly, making the length of the threads a span long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	 Then arrange another delicate silk thread quickly in the sheath and wind it with the first string.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	 Then place your patient's head on a clean cloth.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	 And be close to the sun so that the procedures can be explained clearly, as they are subtle and small tasks. Then insert the needle into all sides at the root of the hairs nearing its end, and pierce it quickly through the paper with care until you work along above the natural hairline;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	 Then extract the hair down to its base, and insert it into the hole, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 Then remove your hand as soon as the hairs reach all sides into the hole with the natural hairline.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	 And if the hole is treated and hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the hole apart by all threads that you have ordered, until the hole appears through and you can see it with the oil of your eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	 Once you draw the bowstring and line up the arrow, clip the oil and let it stay clipped for two or three days until the hair grows back in its place and a callus forms over the wound.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hairs are small, accompany them with long hair from the scalp naturally occurring, and elevate it as you have left it, until they lengthen, then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the inflammation of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	 When this disease known as "aleacrati" occurs in the joint, there are two ways it can happen:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens through sudden wounds, or cuts, or fire-cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And in its treatment, the method is to split that welded joint, separate the lips of it, and insert linen tentacles into it, leaving them until they are healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And it is not necessary to use all methods of treatment for things that dry up and tighten.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	 For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	 but work with things that soften, such as fennel;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 and rosewater or boiled water and flaxseed seeds are cooked, and unguents mixed with any of the oils, and these wrap around a tent, and treat this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	 And the essence of your treatment is to ensure that you do not bind it in any way as it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 and these remedies that we have mentioned are not otherwise than addresses of this disease, so that it does not return as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the clotting substance found within the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness that is actually called "Axacrati," and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	 The occurrence comes from a wound, a tear, caustery, and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	 And for the work involved, you must use a needle, which has a double thread, and the hook is in the hole, and pierce through from the left to right so that the threads reach both sides of the eye.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 Then pull the eye over all the needle, with a thread width of one stratum.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	 And if the shape of the pattern returns as it should, that is good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	 But if not, take the scissors and place them in the tear, turn the pattern, and make two cuts or carve inside the pattern.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	 And the head of the shoulder has two fissures at each angle of the incision you made, and make them into angles so that when they are joined together, it appears as if the letter 'Z' without its crossbar.
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	 Then take the cloth as needed depending on how much it is saturated and unsoiled, like paper, then bring together the two separated pieces with a thread.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then apply what we have said of softening remedies and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	 And if the disease comes from a tear or stitch or cauterization, it is necessary that you make an incision clean of hair on the paper, and according to what has been said above.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	 Then open between the two ribs of a tent as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	 And you must perform the operation according to the form of the illness, for it is very varied in shape, and wise masters devise machines that may possibly restore its natural figure.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 And the patients themselves must do the same, depending on what operation and treatments are required in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	With great care of parchment paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	 When this suture occurs in home-made manner such that the paper above is sealed with the fat of oil and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it does indeed become necessary to puncture a razor beneath the paper, and lift it upwards.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	 And the extent of pressure is applied, aiming to match that which is appropriate for the subtle area, neither too weak nor too harsh, so that the patient does not suffer from an excessively strong or numbing spot.

de l’ungle de l’oil	Concerning the nail of the oil (referring to a method in medieval medicine that involves using an oily substance for treatment)
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	 That the ulcer occurs in two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	 It is of the nature that it seems hard and scaly, and another which is not nervous but appears like frozen damp swelling, so that when touched with iron and cooked in a saucepan, cannot be removed.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 and both types begin near the earlobe, growing slowly until they cover the entire field of vision and all light and eye movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	 And the method of incision is such that the patient places his head on a support, then manipulates the eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	 and lift the paper to your hand, then cut the ulcer edges with small scissors, extending above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	 Then take a needle, and insert hair from a horse, or goat, or ox, and strong thread.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	 Then slightly bend the needle's tip and insert it under the nail. Pierce completely with the entire needle, tie the nail with a thread, and extend above the finger. Shave all hair near the nail that obstructs the puncture, leaving only the root of the skin fold, using delicate motions and small forces; so the body's natural secretion or sweat does not flow through the incision as usual.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	 Never extend to the bone only with the needle and thread, just as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 Then scrape away all the surrounding tissue from which it is formed.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	 And ensure that the tumor does not touch or rupture the skin, and that the pus does not leak out.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 and after making an incision, pour some pearl powder into the wound, and make a paste of lead salve, and leave it until the next day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	 And if the fingernail is not sensitive and you cannot insert a needle, and the knuckles do not fit in, this appearance of a fingernail is often treated with various remedies.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 and as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, work on the patient's side slightly softer, and take a small amount of tumor according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And raise the splinter delicately, and if you see that it does not diminish and there is a swelling afterward, squeeze from your mouth into an oil collier made of litargire and red wax mixed with seal fat, until the next day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 Then resume the other treatment according to this same work, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is opposed to you in the oil, as for abscesses, then wash it out, and cure first the inflamed abscess until it is cleaned, then resume the treatment as before, until it is cleaned.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	 And if the appearance of flesh at the elbow causes great harm in the oil, soothe it with honey and clove, and cut away part but not all, ensuring tears do not come.

des voines des eulz	The veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Red wounds are covered on their surface with oil, and they obstruct the field of view and weaken the eye daily.

de la fistule de l’oil	From the abscess in the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	 They call the wound "Ariassati" fistulas:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers. et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And it is called "sharp head," and made of iron in the same way as described here.

de l’issue de l’oil	From the exit of the nostril
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	 When all nails are pierced entirely without causing harm to the nose or any diminution, it is necessary that you bind the patient.

se ce non;	 If not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If you resume bandaging and dressings and the strain and blisters until it is safe.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The breaking of a veil seen

puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then extract until it is clean.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bow of the joint
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	 This disease called "alcuncatium" is not just water that has gathered in the oil, appearing as if clear fluid descending, and it is not truly such.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	 and the manner of its appearance in surgery is that you make the patient sit on the operating chair properly arranged, then take their head with your hands from both sides until you see the water rise above their hair.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	 Then it must be fixed, and not lowered or elevated, and release the lightness, and show the patient how to do so as usual.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 And if it does not descend on its own, tell the patient that this is acute, and assess whether the bowels are prepared as we have described.

et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. des aigues de l’oil	From the waters of the joints
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	 We have tried similar methods as in water divisions, and what is appropriate for cutting.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 If in practice according to healthiness.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light and sun, and apply strong oil to it.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	 Then place the paper soaked in oil on your left hand if the eye is also turned to the left, or on your right hand if it's also turned to the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	 Then take in your right hand, if the eye is also turned to the left, an instrument called "almadala", or with your left hand if it's also turned to the right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	 Then place the tip of the instrument close to the crown by making an incision with a razor into that part below the lower eyelid near the oil area, then insert the "almadala" gently, and twist your hand until it pierces through the oil layer, feeling when the almadala reaches the empty space.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	 And it is necessary that the width of the Almadian way be at the forefront of the measure of space from the protrusion to the end of the knuckle.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	 and this is its circumference;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 If you see the bone on that paper due to the whiteness of the torn cloth, then place the instrument up to where the moisture is, and express it from one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If water now flows out, then see the patient lying before you with the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	 After resting briefly, if the moisture reappears in the second way, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and does not rise, gently extract Almadian by slowly turning your hand a little at a time;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 And then reintroduce some pus into the wound, and leave the bone inside as it is.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then insert the tube or soft linen soaked in rose oil and abundant honey, and secure with a clean instrument.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 Us and those from our time, insert the camphor paste plentifully with honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	et ou.

et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	 And for the completion of the work, instruct the patient to lie down as they are comfortable, in which place they should rest on their back in a dimly lit area.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	 And they should abstain from all movements, and consume light foods, and do not move their head to the right or left, and remain lying as per their inclination until the third day.

et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And it is not necessary to do this immediately during the treatment or right after the incision now, but you must elevate that area because the swelling rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	 If an abscess occurs, release the pus on the seventh day and apply a dressing to soothe the affected area.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 And when it is calmed, release the scab and place a bandage on your face for one day to keep it covered, and let it remain in that darkened house.

et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And remember that no one should interfere in this case.

de la char sor le neis
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	 Never do they hatch or are there various creatures attached, from which some appear to be scorpions with many feet.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 and if there are any that have hair of such wild colors, and those that have skin of the flesh tone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	 In which case for these creatures that are without hair and not wildly colored, it is fitting to make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	 and work its nostrils, and pour the salve on those creatures, and treat their fur.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Now grasp what you must support at the subtle tip of a finger, as long as you know that entire piece is all bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	 And if there remains anything that cannot be grasped, cover all the surrounding area lightly with delicate movements, so that nothing is left.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	 and without any doubt or abscesses, straighten it as it should be done.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry up and cauterize until the wound is closed and all bones are exposed, then pour oil or wine to cleanse and soothe.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If it does not heal, and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is safe;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	 If there is no puncture as it should be, know that there is softness in the bone above, where strain does not come to cut.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	 Then it is necessary that you insert a flax thread of some thickness and moisten it with your hands, leaving space or less between each one.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	 and place the patient's head with the flax thread at their neck as much as possible, pulling gently until it emerges from within the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	 and this method is often done for children in schools, and it is an easy task for those who perform it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 then hold the head that emerges from the neck with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, feeling each in turn between our flax thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	 Do whatever you know to make the child's bowels pure, then lay them down, let blood flow out, and wipe the string with Egyptian balm, and place it back correctly on their nose as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	 Do this for three days or more until the salves dissolve all that remains of impurity.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	 And then place cotton on their nose for several days until it is cleaned, and if dry medications are needed, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 This is the form of the instrument used to purge the head where one can distill oils and medications onto their nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	 And it is of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cone, and direct them thus.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	 And if you see it, make a tight bandage, and let the extremities be straightened to purge the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And place your hand on the head when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	 Many times emerges at the head a disease called "telulus," which grows and becomes large until it is visible to sight.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	 And therefore you must begin by cutting it off entirely, then use a strong bone saw or burning ointment on the wound.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	 And if it is not cut soon after it grows large, take care to observe if it is hard, of fiery color, and poor in sensation.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	 if it does not yield to iron as it is an encrusted abscess, because when cut once, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 If the abscess is from severe touching, not from sudden color change, and you see that it can be fully covered, if the patient empties his cup and feels no fear while dressing, then treat everything dry and contracted.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut and sutured.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when there is a continuation of discharge from one of these sinew-covered wounds, it brings little benefit and may occur in some men.

et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and then approach the two lips of the incision for stitching, then treat until it heals soundly;

et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez. Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	 The method of suturing is that you assemble the stitches.
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	 or by needles, as we have said in the belly suture;

des apostemes des levres	For abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	 Often happens in the skin abscesses hard lumps, resembling grains of barley, some small and others larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	 Then it is necessary to turn the abscess lumps, split each one with a knife, and pick them up with tweezebrushes and apply to each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 Then place it back after the incision of bladderstone bruises, as long as the wound is closed.

de la char des gencives	From the edge of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	 Often occurs under the gums displaced, which the ancients called "bulbus".

si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	 If it does not return after the fire cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 And these are the forms of abscesses to be covered.
des sordens	Of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	 Never are they gathered at the head of the teeth, between the gums, sores that are ugly and sharp;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	 And never are the teeth black and yellowish-green with pus until the infection reaches the gums, and the teeth become foul.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	 If it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands and his head in your lap, and remove the teeth or sores as they appear, until there are none left.

se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	 If not, begin anew on the second day and the third, until you have regained everything.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	 And know that the teeth need various types of treatments to heal, according to how the work appears, because the razors which do not fit between the teeth have other shapes than those which fit.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 And these forms and others should be made with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	 It is necessary when treating the teeth to delay their pain as much as one can, for they must not be neglected at all.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 because it is a matter of great importance until there are no more reasons to delay the treatment.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient's mouth is strained by chewing, make sure to check for any broken teeth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	 Many times did the pain trouble the patient, and he thought it was or toothache, so he tried draining the bad tooth.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	 And yet the pain did not leave him for this reason, until the illness is over, as we have already tried with such methods.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	 And when you are well-assured of the aching tooth, it is fitting that you scrape around the entire tooth, with strong pressure to protect the gum from all sides;

et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 And let the patient's head be in your steady hands between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth directly with a break, if it does not fall out, take any of these tinctures and put them inside each part lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	 If the tooth is pierced and broken, it must be filled with cloth where the roots are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	 And if gently extracted using pliers, that it does not break when removed.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 It is necessary to work carefully around the gums to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And make sure that you do not break it and leave a piece behind, as this may cause the patient greater pain from the root's wickedness.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	 And be sure not to act as the ignorant surgeon does, who through their haste and boldness breaks a piece of cartilage without restoring it as we have described.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	 but they bring upon the patient great illness from the roots that remain or from the cartilage that is broken, as we have often witnessed.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	 and when the tooth is extracted, wash the socket with wine or boiled water and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	 If there is a spreading of blood, it often happens, to empty the place with vitriol paste.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And if this does not work, then you should cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	 The forms of the tides, wherein one first moves the bones with long points and large masses, do not double when you draw out the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	 and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	They should have large bodies such that they do not bend when extracted, and be well-made of iron, with teeth to grip it firmly.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	 When the root remains when pulling, you must place cotton soaked in butter for one or two days until the area is softened, then put in tweezers called "algofri", whereupon the head appears like a physician's beak.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 and they are bone shaped like files and it is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with all these pliers, it is necessary to expose the entire bone around the root and insert an instrument called "althali," which is a chisel; herein lies its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	 And it is outside and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps from its socket, that is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 If not, assist with all supports, as follows are the forms that come afterward:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two prongs; its form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments used before on teeth and of this instrument which appears to be large pliers, its form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	 And these supports should be strong so they do not break, and know that there are many such dense supports.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	 and similarly of other supports, which may not always be counted.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 and the wise master subtly examines by himself with his instrument, according to his practices and the diseases they indicate; for there are certain illnesses where the elder did not teach any instruments due to their variety, or if it does not break on the cart or other bones, seek the supports that I have mentioned, and assist with the gestures of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	 And they are large and firmly held to grip the bone, that it does not slip out but can be held and removed.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And then restore it to its place with suitable medicine for this case, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then the surgeon possesses all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	 When the tooth appears not in accordance with natural anatomy and its form is unattractive, especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you discern if the root is dead after the tooth, and it is neither on the right nor left, so it cannot be extracted or filed down.
adonques lou raie;	 Then cut the gum.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 And if it is fixed with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is depicted here, resembling a small beak, and made of iron sharp on one end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth becomes harder over time for its hardness and because you dore moving others, and if it is visible that one can file it down, use a part of this file as shown in the shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	 And it is similar to the limb of which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	 and in the limb, one pulls out small pieces little by little until it cannot move anymore.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 then the surface is smooth at the end with no roughness, and if its density is too harsh and it blunts the tongue, one must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it neither dulls the tongue nor disrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth become loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	 When the teeth are loosened by percussion or fall out, and the patient cannot apply pressure to what they bite on without them falling apart, and if you have treated it with constricting medicines, but that is ineffective.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	 If they require it to be bound with a thread of gold, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	 And make the cord neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the bones;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	 And if you see the bones are aligned, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy bones, then place the head between the misaligned bones, continuing until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	 Then resume covering up to where you began, and gently and skillfully pull the hand until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 And secure your ligature at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	 Then wrap the head of the bone with iron wire using pincers, and join them together so they do not irritate the tongue when placed between healthy teeth.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	 Then let it remain as tightly bound as possible for a while, and if it loosens or the wires break, they should be secured with another wire.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 If it stays in place for its full duration, it will maintain the shape of the two teeth and the alignment as if two healthy teeth were present.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	 And when a tooth falls out, you should replace it in its original position repeatedly as we have mentioned.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And only those who are wise and patient should be involved in this process, never shaping it like a cheese tooth; place it where the gap is, securely as we have said, and allow it to remain and serve for an extended time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	And cut off the cord of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	 At no time is this condition which arises from under the tongue or swelling; such as we have seen.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	 Or by accident of a sutured wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	 And the treatments are such that you operate on the mouth with the patient awake and hold their head steady while lifting the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	 Then cut the nervous ligament of the tongue so that it is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or swelling, and this is a sutured wound, then use forceps to grasp the wide ligament.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	 And ensure that the incision is not too deep, near where the artery lies below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	 And once done, lift up a vein of rosy and easily accessible blood, or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 And apply a poultice to the patient each night so their limb cannot settle.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	 And if bleeding persists, then place sulfur on the wound.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	 and if pus emerges, then use a slow-burning caustic agent that is effective for this purpose;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 then proceed with another remedy until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	 and if you observe that the sore is colored or black or hardened, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	 and if it is starting to ulcerate, and there is moisture, then pour the unguent on it, and it stinks of a subtle pus, and cleanses from each side.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	 If blood does not flow into your work, then apply crushed powder of vitriol until it clots, and return to your work as long as you have finished with the wound.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then raise the limb gently and loosely, and treat other ailments until it is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	For boils in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	 Never does food go down the throat that is called "swollen tonsils," and they are properly called two almonds; when you treat them as we have said in the section on it, if they do not heal well, be careful.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 If there are small abscesses of little size and with a hollow feeling when touched, avoid them using iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	 And if they are red with large roots, do not use iron on them either for the flow of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	 But let it lie until it heals, and then you will separate it, or it may break on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is pale in color and the roots are delicate, have an instrument prepared for covering, but first ensure that there are no inflamed areas or lingering irritation.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun with their head exposed and their eyes closed, and have them perform mouth exercises while pressing an instrument between their hands, and press their tongue away from the tool as instructed.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 And it should be made of silver or a delicate copper similar to knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	 You can continue pressing the tongue against this tool and observe any abscesses, if there are any, take a thread-like instrument and insert it into the wound, then pull gently above as far as possible.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	 And from any threads with it, then the cap to the instrument, which is its form, that appears as if by some force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 And so the head is curved, and one place to another, it becomes very sharp, and made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, use tongs for that form which is shaped like it:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	 And it has a sharpened edge on one side and no name on the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And when you have grasped one of the roots, then cut the other in the same manner, and after making an incision gargle the patient with hot water, and warm and soothing liquids, and if bleeding occurs, continue to gardarize the patient with hot water, or boiled quince peels, or mugwort fumes, until the blood stops.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then treat until it becomes well again;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 And no more abscesses appear in the throat other than two almonds, if they heal as do the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was within her throat, which is to say, one small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 and had nearly closed the entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the obstructed passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she remained like this for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had been torn open twice through its two narrow points.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	 So I acted immediately, making an incision in it with a needle, and the pus came out in large amounts.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	 then made another incision on the other side for the small one as well, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	 After inserting a needle into these abscesses, and cutting out a part, no more blood was extracted.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	 And thus the throat duct of the woman was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop treating that abscess for long periods.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	 And the abscesses would return again, filling up the emptied space I had made until it became quite large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	 Then I deceived her and cauterized inside her throat.
ensi demora sens croistre;	 Thus, she stopped growing in size.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 And from these parts I departed, and only God could heal her after me.
de l’uve	The phrase "de l'uvre" translates to "of the work" or "from the work." However, without additional context, it is challenging to provide a more precise translation or interpretation of this term within the text. It could refer to a specific medical procedure or treatment mentioned in the larger document from which this excerpt comes.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	 When they return to the eye, and it becomes swollen and long, one should be called "perpendicular." (Note: This last sentence is somewhat cryptic due to the possible variations in medieval medical terminology. The word "apelé" could also mean "to call upon" or "summoned by",
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 If it is from a large and round source, it is called "yew".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	 When it has been opened as we have said in the cutting method, and the treatment does not help at all, and you see that the abscess wound is soothed, but it is subtle, then it should be lanced.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	 And those that are round and compactly formed, and are not long.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 And if it is bloody or of the flesh-like color or black, then one should avoid its incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	 Therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have described, regarding its width and length, make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press with the instrument that we have previously mentioned.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Then insert the pin through the eyelet, remove it from below, and make an incision as described for removing two abscesses.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	 And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess beyond its natural boundary.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	 because if you cover too much, it will hinder speech and language.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and after the incision, follow as we have said for the removal of two abscesses, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient has fear from covering, then you must apply a method for easing their fear in the process of cauterization.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 The manner of cauterization is acute fever.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	 And it is that the patient places his head in your hand and then presses the tongue with the instrument as described in our book on fire cautery, and rinse with hot water so that it is not too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And with the use of this instrument, here is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	 And it has that you insert or push in the medication with a hair or pipe, as with the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument beneath all the medicine on the vein.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	 and let the patient lie on their side, so that they spit and belch from their mouth of the medication inside, such that it does not come out to the throat, and bubbling.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	 then hold your hand all the medication and press it onto the vein, the quantity of a small hourglass, until you see it working properly and the stinging from the medication is soothed.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	 and if you see it, take cotton and wrap around any instrument, wet the cotton in the medication, and place the instrument into all the cotton down to its base on the vein until the cotn is adhered to the vein.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	 And often do this until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and after IV or V days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	 And if you need to repeat the medicinal cauldration, do so afterward, and around the eye, apply a cloth stuffed with butter, and cleanse what is there surrounding the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And rise up from cold water, and be treated with gargling until it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	 This treatment is more beneficial than the incision, only the cauldration;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	 If it is treated with smoking in this manner, take calamint and wormwood and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of these in a pot, and place over low heat, and let boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 And the piece must be firmly glued with strong clay, and within the vessel there should be an instrument fitted according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	 And it should be of silver or copper, and one of the heads is inserted into the mouth of the patient as long as the vapors rise to the eye through the canal until the vein is constricted.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	 After frequent recurrences, until the vein dries up, and ensure that you do not cause pain at the beginning of the abscess's heating, for many things can happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 and not to act just when it is nearing the stage of hot abscesses.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	 And if this instrument is not present, then take a canal and insert an eagle feather in the head so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 For the crack of a tooth does not greatly trouble the mouth, and it is good together with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	 Many times there are bones or spines from fish in the throat, or anything else.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	 Therefore you must remove whatever you can see and press the tongue to the sun on all instruments, so that you may see movement in the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	 And whatever does not reveal itself and is found in the throat, it must be made to vomit by the patient as soon as possible so that the meat can cook in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	 Perhaps if you extract the thing through vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	 Or perhaps the patient will swallow a piece of sponge, or a scrap from a cloth, or a lettuce root, or a crust of dry bread.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	 And tie to the sponge strip, and then slip it across.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	 And when it reaches its place, if it becomes dry, then you will re-dress the wound.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 and if it does not come to this as we have said, take the instrument of a spatula in this manner:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	 And let the strums be bent over so that they can more easily enter into the throat, and keep the head raised high.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	 and ensure you do not touch the epiglottis so that it does not close, nor push in the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	 and move as if the patient is inserting the instrument themselves, because it should be loose or the place is dry.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 If you have drawn out all of it, or when pulling up with the entire tool until it's dry.
de la sansue de la gorge	And in a similar manner; and then remove without getting deeper; or you do not penetrate further.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	 At no time is there a self-healing without remedy, as I have said in the section on treatment with medicines.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 And when this does not benefit the patient, then you should examine their throat in the sunlight and press their tongue with the instrument I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see this suction, making it resemble all small hooks or delicate pincers that are suitable for such things.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if it is not suitable, then take a twisted rope, and put it in the patient's throat, then make several efforts to pull the rope tightly, doing this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient has water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	 Then take a full glass of cold water and work on the mouth, causing the patient to swallow involuntarily, and move it often with their hand.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 And as soon as he feels relief from the pain, then urinate.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	 And if it does not come out as we have said, then use sage to fumigate the patient with an instrument in the smoke treatment of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 Do this many times, for they will seek their position less aggressively.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	 And the method of fumigation is such that you take an iron vessel where there are coal fires, and it should be covered with a ceramic lid pierced in the middle, and through that opening insert the shoulder of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	 then you pour the fumigation, and have the patient place their cheek in their mouth, and close their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but it rises up to the brain.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	 and now the brain will seek [to be cleansed], and if it does not come out, repeat the fumigametn many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	 and let the patient suffer thirst, and give them salty and sour things to eat, and do not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And then it is necessary for him to go out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	 And the shape of the instrument with which one treats swelling is such that when it can be seen, it appears like bent pincers to enter into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	 and has the appearance of a surgeon's spoon, and it is rough like limestone, such that whatever enters, cannot slip out.
