Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The head can become dislocated or due to humidity, or because of force.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	 And when you have applied the medicine for that corrosion through medicinal treatment, and they prove ineffective, it is necessary to cover that limb up to where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes either by death or malice (witchcraft), which is greater due to the failure of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	 And the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire, and afterward comes the corrosion of members in one member through the whole body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 If you hurry with the covering, and if it is by the sting of certain venomous beasts such as scorpions, snakes, etc., then if the corrosion is at the top of the hip joints, cover them quickly and do not give any space for it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	 And if it comes up to the hand, then protect the joint so that erosion does not reach the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	 And if it comes to the arm, then protect the shoulder.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	 And if it passes beyond the shoulder, it is death, and there are no remedies except for the amount of its usefulness.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	 And so do this when erosion comes or festers:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	 If it comes to the first joint, then protect the other joint after.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	 And if it festers or swells, then protect everything that is affected.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	 If it rises to the leg, then protect the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	 And if it comes over the knee, there is no other remedy than having the patient die from exhaustion.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	 And the manner of using leather or silk on the limb is such that you bind it above and below, extend two sticks one from each side of the binding, and another set of tools to sever the tissue between the two bindings at a width of an inch, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 Then remove the leather or silk and place a linen strip on each side, ensuring that the material does not touch the healthy area, to prevent further injury and infection to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	 And if bleeding occurs while you work, cauterize the wound promptly or apply some constricting powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then return to your medication until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	 And I will tell you what happened to one of us during sickness:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	 It happened a blackness that seemed like scorching fire, and the corrosion first came to his right foot, so much so that it consumed the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	 And when the man saw the corrosion, he hastily cut off the foot with a sword and was saved.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	 And long time afterward the corrosion came to his hand, and it happened to me, and I applied counteractive remedies after bodily cleansing, but could not stop the corrosions.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	 And I vowed to cauterize his hand, and although I did not want to do so, hoping that the remedies would suffice.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	 And he doubted as if I were to cut off his hand, that he would not die, for the vitality of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	 and he despairs greatly, returns to his land, covers up with a coat his hand, and is well again.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 and I have not counted these examples as mere coincidence, but for those who need to know this practice.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	 Never does an abscess occur in the nutritious part, and it remains so long that it causes a great swelling of fistula.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	 and then they protrude and burst, causing the fistula to open up, and remain as if it were a vein.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	 and the skin above is as delicate as fine cloth torn, not reaching bone nor nerve, such illnesses are called "healed," and they are not called "fistulas.";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	 However, if it is so swollen that it reaches almost to the bone at its core, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	 And if the wound is so deep that you must remove all of the flesh, and especially when it is fine, like a fabric.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 and this should not be done due to its decaying nature.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	 And if you suspect that the flesh is hardening, and there is no decay at its core, and the flesh consists of cartilage, then treat with a cleansing enema thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 Check if the breasts are large, and the bowels that are there emit a foul smell; then administer an Egyptian medicinal cleansing enema made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	 Take ease, and oil, and leadwort (litargire), in equal amounts, and put them to boil in a vessel over the fire until the medication turns red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	 And then take as needed according to your necessity, and do it with water and honey, and clyster the chest, and strain the urine.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	 Leave the medication in for two hours, then extract by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	 Do this many times until the chest is reshaped, and it becomes loose again.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	 And never clisterize with water of ashes when this medicine is not prescribed, and that you draw ash from oak wood, pour water over it, then strain the mixture, until you know the chest is properly shaped.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	 And if the patient cannot endure it, neither Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes should be used for clisterization, but use water and honey with some crushed lead.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	 When you cleanse with honey and sweet wine, so that the honey has the property of purifying and cleansing, and the wine makes it holy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	 And when you have done this, and ensured that the chest is well purified, if the suppository causes a stench to arise in it, then take an empyema of roses and oil with wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	 Or you administer a suppository using certain medicines and unguents, of which I have mentioned the properties in treating unguents.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	 And if the opening in the chest is small and nothing can enter through the suppository, slightly enlarge it with a tool, and then insert a tent of Egyptian unguent or basilisk unguent until it expands.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 If the wound is too wide, if the edge and leaves it enough so that the enema can enter there, and if pus with blood flows above, place a cup either higher or lower than where it is located.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	 For when the bowel is in its initial stage, do not leave open sores.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	 And if you cannot cover the chest from beneath as you see, arrange it in such a way that the bowel descends to the lowest place where it is located; because when the bowel is at its beginning, do not leave open sores and if you cannot cover the chest from beneath as you see.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	 so that the bowel descends gently downward, and let nothing remain of the bowel.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	 And take binding medicines to put on the wound, and extend over a linen bandage covering the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	 Then apply pressure to the puncture on the skin that is not more than twice as wide of the first one. Apply ointment under another bandage according to the size of the puncture, and place it over the wound to reduce swelling, without removing the large bandage until after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	 And those who have a puncture on the skin often want to remove it when there is swelling and blood coming from the wound, depending if it's poison or little or enough, digested, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	 And take care if the patient feels pain or numbness and whether there is an abscess or not, and depending on how much medicine has been used, extend it and observe the nature of what comes out at the puncture in the wound, knowing that the vein will heal soon, and approach health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 And then reset it in the morning or after a day, and when you reset the wound, change into another bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are filled with undigested pus after many days, say that the breast is not at ease.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if you encounter subtle corruption after long periods of time, do not despair over health, for healing is nearing.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	 For there are those who delay healing in their wounds by using coal, and others who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	 and suffer from an unhealthy swelling of the breast after many days, believing that the breasts are not affected;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	 and they delay drying of the breasts, becoming protracted, applying nearby medicines composed of moist substances in body but dried in virtue, as with an ointment ending, for there is a significant part of vitriol, and it is this final medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	 Take the ointment that ends with an oil rose, and add the essence of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	 Then you bind it and apply thereon;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	 Then you do the same with it and use it; applying more effective heating when ointments of daffodil are not available, or taking mirra, aloes, and incense, grinding them, powdering them with honey while on a fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	 Then you attach a gauze, extend it over the breast, and never apply an aspersion long-term, using roots of heavenly lily which are similar to barley flour and quinoa.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	 And use simple or complex remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	 Grind them, turn into powder, and put with the honey I mentioned, and apply.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	 If the illness is chronic and not healed by this treatment, then understand that infection has taken hold, causing pressure on the bones or hard parts of the body.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 If the treatment of a fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of abscesses of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Pus is an abscess that arises from under the fingernail of the hand or foot, or sometimes occurs in other areas.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 and when it becomes ulcerated, and is not taken care of, the abscess may develop and run, ooze blood so much until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly consumes the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 And it leads to erosion up to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain and swollen fingers with discoloration.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have instructed in the division, and if the treatment does not help, then one must cut off entirely the excess tissue that is attached to the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 Caustic applications are very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 If the nail then hurries to prick and begin to poke, and bleed, it is necessary that you place your knife underneath the nail causing the bleeding, and lift it upwards, carefully cutting away the subtle vein blood, and apply medicinal substances on fire and corrosive properties to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat with ointments until they are fully healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 And if there is corrosion in the bone, cut it out and treat with fiery remedies, for as long as the bone becomes corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you see the jaw deteriorating, cut into it as previously described, then treat until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 And if it is thrust out and swollen, and it causes great pain, then one must first soothe it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 Then cut the thick hair with a sharp blade diagonally above it, and ensure that the cut does not reach to the bone which is below the hair, as this would cause the patient great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if it occurs, then apply something soothing on top of it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the hand is throbbing.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The dislocations that occur in the shoulders of some men by chance are all flesh, and sometimes there is bone or an epiphysis, but not always, and they do not form at the joint root, where their growth occurs within the shoulder.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 Those who are born with deformity in the groin do not move, and those who are born at the hip joint may sometimes move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The cut for someone who is fat should be light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 Cut it at the base with a wide blade.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	 If you hold with both hands.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one whose shoulder forms afterwards, it is necessary that you first cut round to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate thread, and treat until it is healthy again.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that occur with joint assembly happen by birth, or from a wound's healing process, or from the scorching of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 If it is necessary to treat that swelling, so that the wound heals according to its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 then place between two pads or cloths soaked in oil of roses, ensuring they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 or you put between two thin pieces of parchment while the wound is swollen, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the dislocation comes to either one of its sides with the palm, cut that swelling accordingly as it ought to be.
des vils	 If you are afflicted by evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 These are large sores wrapped and filled with excessive melancholy fluid, which come upon various body parts;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 and more often occurs in the legs of those who walk on stone and work hard, than elsewhere.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you provide no excrement removal at all times, and then the basilica washing of it.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment with iron is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 one is that it's cut and the black blood drained.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 And the other way is to lift the vein, and pull it entirely taut.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The cutting is thus according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 The first leg arises with very hot water, until the large without is sufficiently softened, then hold the leg on the patient's thigh from the hip to the area above the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 Then cut the vein in one place or two or three, with a wide incision, then extract and pull out the black blood into your hand from top to bottom until such quantity as the virtue of the sick can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 And then tie it off, and instruct them to be dyed with black meats.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 And begin evacuation and healing when veins are clear, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The movements of his limbs follow this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 Raise the limb of the patient if there is much hair, then give him a bath, and warm his leg in hot water until it turns red, causing veins to swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 And if you don't have hot water, heat it over fire and then wrap the veins with long cloth at the top of the knee or in the area above the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 Then cover it with cowhide and scrape off the veins from both sides until you can feel them under your fingers.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 And it is seen red and black, and when it enters or passes through skin, it appears as a frayed rope.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Then remove the shaft from underneath the skin, until it is fully withdrawn, and then tie off at the incision site lightly, then cover in another place above three days.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then scrape the skin around the wound until it appears raw, then lift the edges as you have done before, and tie off at another incision site similarly.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Then make another cut or more if needed, then lift it, and wrap around the two pieces of skin, then pull tight up to the second cut.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then extract from incision to incision until it is completely removed, then bandage.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 If you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a strong, double-threaded needle through it entirely, tie the thread securely, push up from underneath the armor, and turn your hand back and forth until it slips out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 And ensure that it does not tear, for if it tears, you cannot pull or lift it, and this causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 And when you have completely pulled it out, place a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil on the wound site.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And dress (treat) until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 And if the vein is twisted and wrapped together and not straight, as we have said, it must be cut lengthwise, but do not seal it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And the treatment is as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The form of iron used to pierce the vein should be curved and not sharply pointed so that it does not cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 and is of considerable thickness because if it were too fine, it would cut the vein; however, let it be large as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	 Of civilized veins.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein should be located in the legs, warm areas or places where no plants or trees grow and on dry land without any moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 and perhaps it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which occurs from putrefaction that comes out of the skin like it happens within the body serpents and worms, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of this vein's beginning are such that a great swelling comes to the leg, then the limb changes, and begins to bleed out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the head is open, it must be wrapped with two pieces of linen about three to four fingers wide along the leg, and leave the swathe in place each time there's no issue.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 And if it is too long, cut off a portion, and wrap the remainder, but do not cover it completely at its root until it has fully come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 because if you cover it, it may re-enter the wound and cause an abscess or decay, and bring about a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 for this reason it must be treated little by little until the head is fully out, leaving nothing or flesh behind.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 and anytime this vein is treated with V or X hands lengthwise, a man came to me after it had been X hands long. When you cut it, it bleeds out one finger or more, and is pierced all the way down to the bottom, so everything flows out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 And let the matter inside be emptied, and restore it with poultices and medicinal herbs for a certain number of days, then treat as abscesses are.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And never strike at this vein with hands or instruments, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or ankle, and much blood flows out.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 then treat as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 From worms that arise between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This illness is known in our land as 'ox disease' because it often occurs within veins and consists of a small worm that develops between skin and flesh, traveling up and down the body. The patient feels intense discomfort from limb to limer wherever the worm goes until it pierces the skin where it moves, releasing powerfully.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 And it is caused by putrefaction of some bodily fluids, as worms and snails and ascarids or belly come.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 And there is doubt about its harmfulness, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance entering, and destroying the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you see it need to be drained or milked, one cannot stop it when it occurs:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 Therefore it is necessary that you bind the area above and below a strong joint tightly, then cut away some flesh and squeeze out fluid, and if he vomits up everything in his stomach, cauterize with fire on top until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 The greatest harm it causes is that it runs the vein, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 and if you see it coming or near the vein, grip its eyebrow firmly, then cut around it, and tie off.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 And the patient must use the cleansing of body parts with soluble medicines for bad humors and wash with rotten meats to purify it.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 From the pain arising from inflammation of blood vessels
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This illness is known in our land as "Vakirir," and causes pain that moves from one limb to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 and I tell you what I see.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to an unwell woman, and discovered swollen arms, with a small inflammation in the veins of her arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 Shortly afterward, the vein rises just as a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything else, like quicksilver when it jumps from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 The pain disperses in that place, and shifts to the shoulder, and then shortly after spreads throughout the entire body, until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then he told me that it turned around within the body, as I have seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	they:
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 Nevertheless, I had wanted to ensure that the pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and exposed veins, so appeared those vapors of constraint.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And they do not appear following this reason for those who are paralyzed, and who have wet bodies and veins restored.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it manifests as we have said, then remove both above and below swiftly, and then close until the swelling subsides back into place.
et cauterize le leu;	 and cauterize at the site.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And if you cannot see it with your eyes, then treat as you would stinky pills and soot pills, along with similar remedies.
des saiettes	 Of arrowheads
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their appearances and the places on the body where they emerge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The variety of them is such that there are some with large points, and small, and hairy, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 And of those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where there are breaks.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 and that which flows in no limb if it leaks by any means:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 or in the principal member (the arm), like the brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it flows in no part of these members, the signs of death that I will tell you hereafter become apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 if it must be that you attempt the extraction of this arrowhead, for death comes in various forms thereafter;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 and when these bad signs do not become apparent, and the arrowhead is not fully embedded, then try to extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 When the arrowhead enters and pierces the bone, causing a cerebral blow that affects the brain, resulting in hemorrhage, swelling, pressure, redness of the eyes, inflammation, tongue redness, mental confusion, and bile vomiting.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 And sometimes without strength in the nose or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 And occasionally affecting speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 The wound with white moist flesh resembling hairs, and healing like the redness of coal.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 If these signs appear to you, provide treatment, and remove the arrowhead if it is not deeply embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 The signs of the arrow when it enters or exits are as if they were close to the left breast, feeling as though it had been embedded in a hard object, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 And sometimes it moves like hairs do, resulting in black blood coming out, accompanied by chills and cold sweat, leading to fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 Then he has doubt that death will come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrowhead is that there are no traces in the wound's exit, and the throat swells, and the patient changes complexion, and breathes deeply and seeks cold water.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 And if the arrow falls into a cavity near the ribs, it is close to small intestines;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 and pours out much blood and causes great pain and sighing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 and they move all the limbs of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	heuze d; 1 (h: they s of gk: MDP.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrow pierces the belly and does not burst out through the intestines, there is no hope in treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 And if the arrow falls into the bladder, causing it to leak and frequent urination, the patient feels strong pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 You say that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, depending on how they are made and the collarbone and throat and shoulder and upper arm and spine and ribs and hips, and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it's not poisonous, as I will tell you how it happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 It happened to a man whose arrow fell just below the eye socket near its root:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I tried it, and on the other side removed the grease from the ear, and was found to be completely healed.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And he removed an arrow from the fat of the ear below the skin and paper, and the arrow was reinserted, but could only reach the tip towards its base, and it was a large Turkish bow without any iron except for the ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The joint was healed, and nothing adverse occurred to him again.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 And I removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an Arabic bow with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I dealt with the Saracens and carefully handled it as much as I removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And when an arrow is lodged in one's body, where it has reached the belly, thinking that he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 and then after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I cut near the arrow, skillfully manipulated it, successfully withdrew it, and there was no harmful outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 And if you see a person to whom an arrow has fallen on the back, and his wound is freshly dressed above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 and if the arrow remains within him, not disrupting his natural state or causing harm in any of his natural functions;
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And when you see another man to whom an arrow has fallen on the face, and his wound is dressed above;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 and it remains in such a way that they suffer great pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	 And many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And he suffered from an arrow in his forehead among the nobles at the king's court, which was somewhat tilted to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 and the arrow was fully embedded (or 'set back').
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I went for treatment after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 I removed it with all subtlety and did not feel anything (or 'it didn't hurt').
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 and there was no pricking or pain from his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was the tip of the arrow that caused this. So I applied a warm poultice with soothing and digestive properties because his eyes were not swoln.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 and then it seemed to me that it was an arrow wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 The next day I applied the embolaster to his hands and thoroughly dressed the wound, allowing the patient to endure thus for a long time until he felt the arrow in his nose.
et il le me dist.	 And then he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I applied the medicinal acid to the wound until it was healed, and tested it, feeling the head of the arrow dissolving in place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 then I reinforced the opening of the wound with that medicinal acid until the head of the arrow became clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 and it traversed fully within four months, then I loosened the edges which I had clamped with pincers, on both sides, but could not be removed.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 Then I ceased to subtly and ingeniously devise methods of reduction, until one day it was taken in hand well-made pincers, according to the form that will appear at the end of this chapter, as long as I treat it, and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And they judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 Then I shall reset it accordingly, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 And I have told you the quality of arrow extraction, so that you may focus your care on what I do not mention here, for the book cannot cover everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 but the wise master physicians say a little about many things and that which is present and failing, nine works are done, and nine instruments are used in dealing with strange matters arising in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows do not exit from limbs where they are deeply embedded but according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 or through the same opening or by another way.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and that which exits where it entered is an arrow entering living flesh, and never exits more than once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not exit now, let it remain as long as the flesh is rotting around it, and be swollen at the point of entry.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 And similarly if it is lodged in the bone and cannot exit, let it remain so for several days, moving slightly each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And then if it exits, and if not, make a very fine hole around it until the flesh is loosened, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 When the arrowhead is embedded in the bone of the skull and approaches one of the brain's cavities, and some of the incidents I have mentioned above afflict the patient.
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If it cannot be drawn out but left until it is even after some days, for if the arrowhead reaches this point, it causes death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 If the arrowhead is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the fascia, and the patient remains without any harm for several days, then proceed with attempting to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed thusly, administer remedies around it as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the wound until it is sound.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 And if the arrowhead is back in its place within the body so that one cannot see it, then wrap all around it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 And if you feel it, use any suitable instrument to remove it.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 And if you cannot for stretching the wound, and piercing deeply into the arrowhead, there being no bone or nerve or vein, then bleed as long as the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 And treat the arrowhead if you can, and if it has ears on which it grips, then apply a sticking plaster that is firmly set in two parts to what you can move, and then break or bend the ears of the arrowhead as much as you can.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And subtly ensure that you do not break the arrowhead, but pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, lift up to the nearest resting place and then draw it, as pulling might relieve the strain of extraction.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 And if bleeding occurs in the opposite direction, apply as we have said of treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 And watch over the incision of the nerve and vein, and devise a method as you would draw out an arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And place the patient as they were when the arrow fell on them, for that is the greatest help you can provide; and if you cannot do so, then place them according to what their signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrow that comes from another direction, or where there is no visible injury, or the skin is swollen in that area if you can see or feel it distinctly.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Therefore cut accordingly as long as the pincers can grip, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	 If it is still present now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if [the arrowhead] is caught in the bone, twist your round hand, until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot exit, let it remain for now, then resume extraction until it fully comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 and if the arrowhead remains in place, remove it entirely from the body.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 and if it comes loose while administering the cautery, if you use a tool with a sharp point, then the tip of the arrowhead enters into the handle of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 and then remove it entirely; if the arrow is loose, put the tool with an inward-pointing tip to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrowhead is touched, it is necessary to cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 And if the arrowhead pierces or hits the belly or bladder or ribs and is recent, you must apply pressure there.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And guard against puncturing the vein and nerve, then extract it, then close the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And continue the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and this one looks like this:

grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 large, various, and small, depending on the quantity of the arrowheads.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The form of the forked beard is also like that of a bird's feather, to thrust at the tip of the arrowhead, as here shown.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pincers for pushing and probing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 There are veins to be opened numbered thirty-one, from which sixteen heads emerge, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 Two battens located behind the ears, called "herbecs":
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 And two arteries visible in the temple areas:
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 And two veins located in the upper lip area of both lips, called "aspiers":
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 And the vein that is above the forehead:
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 And the veins that are near the neck.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 And the two nerves which are there, above.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 And the veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are called "aquae ducts.";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 And two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins of which there are five in each arm commonly found:.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 One is the cephalic one, and it's on the left side, called "the principal vein" or "voinnes du chef".;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 And the middle one is called "fast", and it's composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, referred to as "the body's vein" by some. ;
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 And the basilic vein is on the right side, called "the belly's vein", and it's above the fossa, clearly visible near the armpit when observed. ;
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 And the savior is the vein located between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it has two heads.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 and in the leg where there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 one is from below the hollow of the left breast muscle, and the second saphenous vein which is at the right ankle joint.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 and the vein called "nesse," that is in the ankle of the other leg.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 and on the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The pain from the veins that are behind the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 Et the quality of the ointment, as I have told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub their head or veins with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 Then tighten the neck of the patient with a tourniquet so that the two veins appear behind the ears at two levels depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 Afterward take hold of them by your thumbs and where you feel hair growing from above your thumbs, be careful.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lancet, and insert it just above the vein until the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein towards its origin, cut through both sides of the skin tract, ensuring clear cutting of the vessel, allowing blood to flow as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then strain and bind it until it is well aligned;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 And I have already mentioned the incision and caustic in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The cleaning of the two veins that are in both temples, if they have been swollen for a long time, and hardened, and ulcerated from habitual use, and cause tears to flow on the sides.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 and the quality of such cleaning is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 and it's that the patient must stretch their neck so that both veins are clearly visible.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 and they feel pain under your thumbs, then tie them off.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then lift the skin over the vein under your index finger and insert the lancet below it, and lift the vein upward, and tie it off, just as you did with the other two veins, and bleed according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 Then dislocate the patient's limb, and place your two fingers on the vein for an hour, then place a cotton pad.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is cleaned.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 And we have spoken of their comforting and extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The cleansing of the veins in the forehead is worth as much as the cleansing of the cerebral vessels for ancient face diseases, and migraines, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 and the quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 then take the instrument called "auger," whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place the point over the vein, and press with your hand or another object, allowing the blood to flow out according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Then loosen the patient's neck and bind the vein so that it is straight and not widened with any cloth or bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 However, it must never be too tightly wrapped.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 and the vein is twisted, because the bone is near, and by chance it may break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The veins in the two forearms should be tied up at the elbows, wrists, and joints, and with skin conditions on the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 and the condition of their veins should be such that the patient loosens his neck by twisting any bonds.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then cleanse it, and let the wound heal completely with some length of fine thread that is somewhat wide, as there is no need to tighten.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 And if the sutures are delicate, they may sometimes tear;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 then apply sufficient blood to what is needed, and then cover with gauze, and wrap it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The healing of the wound is not to be hindered by cold or sweat, and other skin diseases such as migraines and rashes that occur on the face, especially when it's longstanding.

et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 And do not go too far with it, and follow correctly along the blood according to your need, then let her rest one night, for she is often quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 And this is the form of the phlegm:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The bandaging of the II joints assists in stretching of the limbs, and at the onset of measles, and many diseases, and impetigo, and erosion, and herpes, and itchiness.

et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 and the master stands above the head of the patient, and the patient cuts slightly over one seat, then let the vein bleed a little bit widely, then stop the blood timely, or as much as necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 Then redo on the other side of the vein, then realign the joints, and compress the veins moderately so that the patient is not strangled.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 And leave it until morning, that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the liver ailment called jaundice
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleaning of lice from the lips helps to clear infection in the mouth, and gum disease, and cracks on the lips, and bad breath and itching.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 And the quality of healing depends on making the patient sit in front of you and tightening their neck as I have described.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 Then turn the lip and look at the veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be identified by their blackness and the small dark vessels around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 So do both, and if you do not recognize them or have doubts, cut the larger one from each side, and likewise with all the veins above and below, as it is of the same kind.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the jaundice underneath the tongue

et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 and its quality of bleeding is such that the patient cuts between his hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks down each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 Then you should bleed both [veins], but not too much at once, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The veins of the elbow that we commonly bleed are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 or by gripping all of the forearm firmly wide apart, or with an olive-shaped and sharp instrument like scissors; called "anchisile.";

Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of this mistletoe plant is much renowned and very broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 And it is necessary to open clear veins with visible blood, and that contain much blood and impurities;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 and this is the form of an olive bubble:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is finer pointed, and meant for collecting subtle veins, where there is a subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The vessel of the veinous network, which is one of these veins, helps in diseases that are from under the throat, and neck, and sides, and belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 And it is fitting for the vessel to be filled adequately, and that it cleanses from the artery which lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 And if he pierces the artery, and bleeding occurs, then it should be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And it must not be pierced by the flame, but cut as one shears.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 And if the vein does not open clearly, you should extract it and use another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 or if you wish to avoid any blood from it, or you find it in place within the arm vein:
elle apert manifestement;	 it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 and the vessel is sheared by flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 And if you know the place of the vein, then as I instructed you to extract it and move away the arm, touch its location until you feel the hairs.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 Then signify the place with a mark, and then lay the arm, and shear the vein by flame as one shears.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 And ensure you do not injure the artery when you see it swollen, for it is the artery.
eschui la donques.	 Then escape quickly.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 And if you see it protruding upwards like a child's urine, and the wound is red and slender, know that it is from an artery.

et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And be in fear, and do not move the limb until it is safe.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if the wound is not blocked and it bleeds, and there are no medicines at hand, clot the artery should it open, for the head of the limb retracts.
et estainche li sans.	 And he becomes numb.

se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 if he is numb, that's good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that numb the blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 and the numbing is not harmful in most cases for a slight location of the wound, and possible flexibility at the joints of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The cleaning of the vein helps in bleeding from above and below because it is composed of basilica and cerebral substances, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 and it behooves the saigneror to wash out the nerve beneath it, and if too much is taken, and they sever the nerve, which swells and causes severe pain, and perhaps cannot heal.
