et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 And remove the nerve with your hand.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is no touch it the veuine, then they are l'a cauterisee.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The cerebral sinus helps, attracting blood to the head, and aids the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 It is customary to heal in pinching the flax oil or myrtle vein, as it's the most effective of all leeches, because there are no nerves or arteries there.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 Nevertheless, one must seek the lighter ones and avoid causing pain during the first treatment, then repeat it.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 And sometimes it enlarges the glands in some men when doing it for the first time, but does not cause pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you must know about healing is that the cure is not performed soleebut to maintain health and prevent future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 And there shall be the sinew made within one of the three veins mentioned above.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 This is to know, cephalic, saphenous, and basilica [vein types].
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 And it should be sinewed at the beginning of summer and autumn after eating, and in winter when signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 And it should be sinewed on the first day or third, two hours or three days later.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The sinew treatment for diseases has no set time, but when needed is by day or night, at all hours and always.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 And it does not require sinewing for children up to fourteen years old, nor women pregnant in their seventh month onward.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not let them raise their hands who are old, those who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 When anyone wishes to heal themselves in any way, it is necessary that they clear the intestines with a gentle enema if there is much feces retained so that excessive waste does not harm the main body parts.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 Not even those who are too fat from meats or drunkards, no matter how severe their condition may be.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 and heal after suffering from colic, vomiting, abdominal distention, frequent intercourse with women or men, insomnia, waking up often, and whatever else weakens the body, whether by a thing of the weapon or in the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 then subtly remove the humors if it is heavy with meats and drinks and medicines, provided that you have them to spare.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 Then use a bath if nothing hinders it to refine the blood and cleanse the vein around the area of the third finger as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 And protect yourself from work, pain, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 Be bound and elevated, and the healer's hands should be higher than that which is being treated, then rub the arm two or three times, then gently remove the bandage for a moment because if it is too tight or too loose, one cannot cure it properly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 Then rub the limb with hands until the veins swell and he can feel them.

des sainies de ventouse	 And of suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Vents are made of horns, or ivory, or glass.

ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.

ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 When she feels feverish, or shows signs of heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 And bloodletting which is done by cupping and blood extraction if performed on fourteen points of the body, causing one to be completely bald.

et les ventouses des II jambes;	 And cupping at both legs.
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 And cupping at both ankles.

et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And it is not necessary that she be treated with heat or any burning, in no disease arising from congestion until the whole body has been emptied.

Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amartine or balm of Gilead, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 If one whom you treat has a tender and broad chest, there is no need to put oil on it, but after ventosation with rose water or cold water, or blackthorn water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture should get up easily, or use myrtle water, and sumac, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those who have large excess fluids rise with old wine, or of watercress water, or of fennel or chamomile infusion, or similar substances.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 and they should not fasten the bladder with a cupping session before or during the bath, but after the bath one or two hours.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 and they should not sleep after cupping therapy, and it is necessary that they bathe when they need to be cupped and after being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 And let those who are prone to constipation take this, and their stool is too hard and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 If it is necessary to apply cold things such as ripe pomegranates and endives and lettuce at ease, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 and mince pieces, and lard of bacon, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And those with cold constitutions should take honeyed syrup and fragrant wine that is neither old nor new, a little mince meat, minced pieces, small birds, and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 and each day when he refreshes himself, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 and it is appropriate to give certain individuals triacle or muskat before the incision or afterwards, to strengthen the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 and ensure they are filtered, but only those who are ill should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The ventouses that are applied without using heat are those placed over the liver, and joints such as gout, podagra, and also on the abdomen, buttocks, knees, and elbows, because these members cannot be pricked in any place, and it is done only to draw blood from one member to another, as we do with the nipples when they are not well.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 To remove the swelling in the limb, as we apply ventouses to the abdomen and buttocks to reduce the size of the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 And alleviate the pain when there is congestion or stone, and if possible draw it out by its attracting power occasionally the congestion, or remove the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 And thus it is done when placing it over the liver and spleen where there is retained windwassering, and these blisters are made hollow to drain sufficiently.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 And they are not made together with fire, and never flat from water, as in the case of diseases causing pleurisy, and thus you fill the blister with hot water poultice or warm water after boiling medicinal herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with heat is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And it must be two fingers wide and half a palm thick at the base, with a small hole near the middle like piercing with a needle, and made of woolen cloth so that it does not slip off when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 And have at hand a staff of crossbar from reed or iron, to place a candle holder, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and condition of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 Because children's bloodletting vessels are different from adults', and thin rather than fatty.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And one should thus place this bleeding vessel on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 take the candle of wax or ointment, and place it amidst the bleeding vessel across the crossbar which is midst the bleeding vessel, so that its glow reaches to the bottom of the vessel without burning the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 and then place it upon the limb, and your fingers should be above the puncture site as we have said, so that when one wishes, steam will arise, and the bleeding vessel is removed.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And straighten it as before, and often repeat if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the cupping therapy used for diseases of pleurisy, there is neither a rod nor tube, and it's only made when filled with liquid, and placed on the limb.
et c’est li forme:	 and this is how it works:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Cupping therapy is only applied to limbs where regular cups cannot be used due to their small size, such as lips and gums.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 And for other bare areas like the scalp or neck.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 And the quality of use is that when you find cups filled with gently flowing clear liquid, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 And they place it on an acute wound with gentle warmth until it becomes familiar, and has nothing in its belly.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 And then apply bandages of veins and compresses, then rub the limb until it is reddened, and place poultices on it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are full and ready to burst, if there is a place where one can apply compresses, then do so, for it works very well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, lift the swelling gently and then apply water, very thoroughly, and then squeeze it out.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the limbs are not too sore to touch after applying poultices, then apply a clean linen cloth soaked in cold water and place it on, until the swelling is reduced.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 And if blood is multiplied, put it on crushed vitriol or gallnuts, and similar things, until it stops.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 Or you put a half-moon of peeled beans on it and let them sit until they become dry, thus stopping now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if more is needed, then take other medicines.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the medicines do not take hold, then rub the blood freshly and insert a needle until it stops bleeding, and then place them on top of each other, and as soon as they feel the blood, let them dry.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they are leaking, then powder some aloe and silex broken or ash upon it, and they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These treatises are often necessary in the art of medicine, and they restore broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Learn this, dear scribe, that the foolish seeker delves into this chapter, never having seen any ancient books or letters read.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 and for this reason is strange knowledge in our land, for I have never found any good ones;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 and I know nothing else, though by the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I am familiar with the subject, through experience, and by habit throughout my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 And I have described in this chapter what is contained within it, and abbreviated at the end, and clearly shown the forms of tumors that are created, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say that the preamble of this book contains the essence and wisdom of its chapters, so those who are experienced apply their understanding to truth, allowing them to know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs to any limb, it is necessary for you to support the injured part on both sides if nothing completely supports them, as in weakness of arms, children, or old people.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 If the tension is not too great, or too cold.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 And consume cold foods such as cold joints of meat, and fowl or veal, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill oneself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you are no longer doubtful about a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 If the patient's condition returns to its first state that they previously used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that cause swelling or viscosity, such as boiled wheat, rice, eggs, beans, veal, chicken, fresh fish, and strong wine, along with similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	When with gradual dislocation, movement is soon followed by fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that broken and old bones cannot be well mended or joined according to their natural character for healing of limbs, nor those as well who are too tender, like the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 But do not worry, reset over the broken bone with strong tendons that are taut and join the limb together, until it is as strong as before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And do not leave all his work undone, and for this reason he must nourish himself with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	by the bolejles Que c; If you say b: OU; ça finge t m and so et se ou n'ilz ne bon line: Ca: Jarn’s.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	When the break of the head is different from the break of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all types of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that go with rotation, and others by bending, as the length of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture accompanied by a tiny split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And each person has his own method and proper instrument for restoration, according to what comes to mind in their place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 and is known the bone fracture by how it is twisted, and opened widely at the break, near to the press of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 and when there is no twist or touch it, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 But it may well have twisting, or tearing, or small breaking.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move your hand at all, but apply the medicines that come next and then gently hold it in place.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And know that if the breakage protrudes outward and the two parts are disjoined, they must now be aligned evenly, as with abscesses when they come forth.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 and if abscesses occur, leave it untouched until the abscess is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 then make it equal to movements that you can gently and easily perform, knowing that the restoration of this is easier than those with missing parts.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 then bind it as necessary later on.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 And if the bone is broken into pieces and consists of two parts, whether hands or feet, or to your hand with small limbs, or to both tendons, or to one tendon and to your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 And place the limb according to its natural shape. So when the parts of the broken limb are severed, carefully realign them using all methods to put the fractures back in their places as you can move them, and ensure that with your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And well align the two heads of bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 And feel carefully with your hand if it seems that they are not aligned properly:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 If the dressing is done well, and do not extract it too much or press as those who cause abscesses hot and contracture in the member have witnessed many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 And when the limb is at a standstill, treat the patient well so that they do not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning, or in any other manner.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And ensure that the limb is so secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For when it feels no pain, not even slightly, and one must place it in such position that it feels no pain at all.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 and ensure that it is placed correctly, so there are no twists when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 and the quality of the broken limb should be according to what I tell you.

Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small bones, such as ribs and thighs:

puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 Then lie wraps light gauze, three or four times around the limb, and secures it with a little bit of the entire bandage, then goes above the fracture and tightens less than the fracture site, gradually moving away from the fracture.

puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 Then return to the part below the fracture, and restrain it gently, not too much nor too little, as we have said in the first section above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Then place between the splints linen or cloth so that they are all equal, then bind everything above it with bandages, and then place well-made supports underneath, unless there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing on the abscess heat and which draws out the swelling, leaving it as such for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 Then restrain with your supports, and they should be a piece of cloth cut one hand's width wide, or wood used for making battens, or coconut fibers, according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 But it is necessary for the splint placed over the break to be a bit thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 and also as long as needed for the member, whether small or large in size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then fasten between the splints just as you did on the first one, and above with a thread quickly, like in the first plastering over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 the tighter it is above, the less there will be.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and it must be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 because if the thread is too thick, like the work of those who twist flax for linen cords, it causes great error, as the plaster cannot be evenly distributed if it's too fine, and there should not be less than two spaces between each splint.

And if the patient is in pain from the shoulders of their extremities after being strained into place, then apply cotton or raw wool rags beneath them so they do not slip.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the head is broken, I will tell you the remedy for this below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not happen to pull out all the bones of a limb broken on the first day.

et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 And use here the method of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twisting injuries:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 And take flour that is kept near the mill walls and mix it with abundant egg, then create this concoction, which should not be too clear or too thick, and use it; this is the common method of plaster for restoring fractures in various positions, especially in women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another way of plaster to restore fractures, dislocations, and twisting injuries:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take lion's blood, aloeswood, onions, asafetida, gum arabic, and myrrh, one part each.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 Mirror and aloes, five parts each.
alechil VIIII З.;	 Alecsei VII, nine parts each.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 And make powder, and the honey with wheat flour;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 If the body's constitution is hot, use this emplaster, for it has good composition and quickly repairs broken bones, benefiting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another way of an emplaster that works well with sprains:

mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 Mirri oil and aloe, soaked for IX hours.
acaice VI З.;	 Here comes the first of six chapters;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 And here begins the first of six parts; it is boiled and well mixed with water or whey, and given to drink.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another method for treating dislocated joints and bones that have come out of their place; it alleviates the pain occurring, and is used to cut through the bone and fracture.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take fresh linens, and make them soft with oil heated in it, and place on top of the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These plasters do not heal but are good to soothe of hot abscesses and properly alleviate the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another method to restore broken bones;
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves and leaves of the earthly poppy; grind them together, and make a poultice with it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to reset the healing of broken bones and reduce remaining abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take root of valerian, chamomile flowers, violets' petals, and equal parts of wheat flour from each.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 And grind it, and crush with wine, and if the limb is swoln, then crush with fresh water of coriander or just water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way to treat more effectively than the first, when an abscess comes to heal the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take roots of valerian, and flax seeds, bladderwrack, poppy seeds, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, in equal parts.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 And grind it, then crush with salt water or fresh water, or wine, depending on the heat of the limb and its resting state.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that one should not put anything other than a mixture of wax and oil on a broken limb for healing, except if it is too soft or too hard between two layers.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems like Galen suggests that on a broken limb for healing, one should use dry substances that are somewhat warm, such as myrrh, frankincense, and similar things, as we have mentioned before.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another way to treat injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Take mucus and sheep's liver, or feathers of birds, and valerian, in equal amounts; grind them, make a poultice, and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 And then slightly move it again afterwards, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has moved the bone from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 If so, do not attempt to relocate by hand alone.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 And if pain comes at the place, or itching, feeling of relief, or swelling occurs, hurry up and relocate it, and remove the splint now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 and take light gauze, and wipe with damp sponge, and immerse in cold water, and lift up the place, until itching ceases, and pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 then let the limb rest for an hour, and apply a dry linen or woollen cloth immersed in cold water or rose oil, and bind it to a stool until you are sure of heat from an abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 Rest the inflammation of the limb, and there is bone pain, then resume subtle movement, and a bit of plaster, and do not stretch it as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And carefully until healed completely.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and warm and painful and swollen, and you need opiates and linen, then reset as before, similarly to how it was done initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if there is no improvement in the limb as we have said, do not reset it unless after three or four or five or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 and no more than twenty days as seen, until the fracture heals, approaching joint alignment with a charm underneath.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 then reset it firmly, and the flesh grows thicker as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 and if you see that the place dries too much, know that no infection can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Rise from warm water baths as you feel the need every day, and lightly dry yourself once a week.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 Therefore, in this practice, you should cut off the gangrenous tissue from the limb and quickly remove what fools do to wrongly set bones that twist the limb back on.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 It is harmful, and in such practices there is fear, I see no other than the lazy ones and those who work directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 There are many ways to fractures, diverse forms, and their causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 because there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the joints break through all the bone until the marrow comes out, just like with an axe or stick.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 And for this reason is called this manner of fracture "chiñure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 Or the sword pierces the bone above without sense and is called this manner of fracture "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 And there are wounds from these two large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impacted blow, crack, neck bone fracture, or fall onto the spine, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fissure that reaches the tunic which lies below or above the bone, where the wound may be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And if there is a wound that closes in the bone as fine as a chamois's fur, and it is a small crack, and for this reason called this fracture "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 And if the wound is made by arrow strike or falling, or similar things, and causes the bone fragment to descend, it looks upwards as when smiths heat their forges.
si entre li piere dedens.	 If between the stones inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this occurs especially in those who have moist bones at their heads, as with children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 and it happens in all these ways of fractures where small parts are separated as elements;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all types of fractures by displacement underneath them, and the incisions on sinews, and by the corroded cartilage which is beneath.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	And they; (et d do not as he sonte t and ous le trementd; that are the ou pr* est: S, so it.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, beware of accidents to the patient, and if you see any bad accident such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, fever with chills, eyes protruding and turning red, and other similar dispositions, cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeful accident, and expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the suffering comes first to you, and it is in winter, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day when you can move it.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is like this, and you remove the bone within seven days, so that the tissue under the bone becomes corrupted, then come the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the bone fracture reaches near the cloth that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part thusly:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 and it is that you grasp the wounded head firmly, and expose to the bone in all ways possible, and on top of the wound's appearance, as smoothly as you can, if bleeding occurs upon exposing the bangle or vein, aid with what is necessary, and ensure you fill up the space with scrapes soaked in oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 And make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, ensuring that the blood flow improves.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 Then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of treatment:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 One method is that you cut narrowly in front, which is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second method is that you have various cuts of different widths, some narrow and others wide, which are pointed, and made with iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 and work lightly so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 And if the bone is rough and hard, it is necessary that you perforate around it, making cuts with tongs, not too deep so they don't penetrate beyond the skull, and there should be a margin or circle above the point where it does not pass through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 And it is necessary that you have several things at hand when each comes into its place on the edge of the bone, so that you may have tools for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 and there are the forms of three kinds of tools:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality for cutting near the bone broken is that you place one tool on the bone and turn it until you know the bone is cut.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 then place the tool elsewhere slightly afterward and do so all around it, and with the incisors cut out the space of the bone that is between the fractures, doing this more delicately than you can, gently, as we have said, until you pass through the bone to your hand or any one of the tongs that you have like pliers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 And ensure you do not touch the brain or the spleen.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 And when you have pierced the bone and created an opening, it is necessary to reset the readiness that has been delayed from the bone to any other instrument resembling a chisel; however, it must be more careful and finer than the other chisel.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 and if there is nothing delayed from the small bones or scales, gently move them with slight movements;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 Then treat the wound with sutures and ointments as we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And another method of treatment is that which the Greeks (Galinians) describe, which is more effective.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 and it holds much strength, and this is its nature.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose the bone part where the break opens up; and once you have exposed that part, then place atop the blade of this crescent-shaped incision tool, which has the following shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And does not cut cleanly on one side, as the affected area has swelling in two directions, so that the cutting is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 then place a small mallet above it, so you tap lightly around the entire bone, and ensure you are careful not to damage the cloth that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 if it is loose near the bone, so you gently tap the bone, because we do not want to harm it much or cause fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce all the way through to the skin and is cut only from above, with small fragments remaining, you should attend to that sharpness again, and remove the scales with a fine razor in which various quantities must be used, so as to apply most appropriately to each location according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you approach from great heights, then proceed with more subtlety, and continue in this manner until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of these other haircut treatments and delicate fractures, it is necessary to reset according to its proper alignment.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 And this is something that has not been redone by those who have dedicated their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the patient's face is revealed, it is necessary to take a cloth of flax according to the amount of the wound, and oil with rosins, then apply to the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 Then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers and oil with wine and rosins, and place it over the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 And do so more gently as you can, not to burden the face, then apply above it another bandage, and do not tighten it too much until only the wound is covered.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 And leave it thus for one or two days until the abscess is soothed, then release it, and administer medicines as listed roots, flour of vetches, powdered incense, aristolochia, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 And from these substances make a powder, and apply it to the wound, and administer such medicines without causing burning.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 And guard that the wound is thus clean, not leaving any ointment or allowing a boil to form there, for when a boil forms on the tissue of the brain, it hurts and becomes inflamed, bringing great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 For when one applies something caustic there, it corrodes just below.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, should any unfortunate event occur to the patient as we have mentioned, it is doubtful and uncertain.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 If darkness does not come due to the medicine applied, and its power prevails, then it is necessary to take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and woolen cloth, and place it on the sore.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then care for in ways as needed until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 Know that at no time are the two parts of the neck broken or separated by one from another, for they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 and that which is behind is cartilaginous and does not break or twist, it simply supports and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should tie your little finger or thumb behind the neck, and place the break equally into your index finger's knuckle, and use a pouch for safety until the neck returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And do this gently, ensuring the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose and cannot bring the finger to its place, it is appropriate that you put a little bit of grease on the top of a small stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 And if the fracture is of two parts, do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If not, after the seventh or latest day, when the abscess has calmed down, then bind to the neck with narrow strips of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 Or you bind another from a different side, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 and the strips should be wide enough to fill the neck opening.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And each healer says one must grease the wounds with butter, and change it every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they be made from fine wool and flour powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 Then leave the tent intact as long as the bone is fixed, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And never place an eagle's feather in the tent opening, and if it is near the window screen, prevent any breakage, and blow air to repel foul smells.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 Or do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the patient while you work on it, then put some grease or cotton wool in oil roseate, or a small portion of diacron.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 And if an abscess does not open, then apply plaster promptly: wheatmeal paste mixed with goose egg yolks and frankincense powder, then cover with light gauze, but do not bind the feathers.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 and if the feather breakage is minor, with small broken pieces, extract the spicules appropriately for this, then close the tear, and mend other irregularities such as charred or burned areas, and apply suitable plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he has no wounds in the eyes, treat with bandages and apply compresses of warmth until they are well again.
de la routure de la mandibule	From the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated and there is no resulting wound, the fractures are not severe, nor are they broken in two, unless the inner part has swelled, which can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the mouth of the patient.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 and if the fracture is on the left mandible, put your index finger from the right hand, gently press the fracture, and shape it with the other hand as needed, making it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced by two joints, it should be that you make an adjustment with a length equal to the parts.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 And if there are movements of the axis or rotation, strain with a thread made of gold or silver or silk, then place a padded cloth on the fractured jawbone, and cover it with two layers of fabric.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 And place upon the drapelet a large well-made pillow, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and lay it along with movements that you can make, instructing the patient to rest, and serve light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 And if you see that the form changes, reset it daily for three days, then return it to its original position once changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 And apply an emplaster on top, with finely ground powder or flour from sorrel, after you have removed the catheter.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 And place a light linen over the emplaster, and if the emplaster hurts, ensure that the patient's position does not change until healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 Many times are healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And when abscesses appear, treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 And if there is a fracture and wound together, ensure no piece of bone remains unhealed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 If the subtlety of the broken tibia has not healed yet.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, enlarge it gently according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have extracted all these pieces of bone and it no longer remains in the wound, then dress the wide wound, and place on fine stitches to close it up until it is healed.
de la forcele	(tirq; If: C.n's." est s.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The severe fractures occur many times before, at the shoulder, and the fractures are of three kinds:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 Or it is broken into two parts, with fragments, and it is the easiest to mend.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 Or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the treatments are such that when there is a fracture with a wound, you have two assistants, so one treats the shoulder that feels the severe fracture.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 And the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 Then make equal the break to your legs so that it forms as it should, with no visible deformity or discomfort.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you need to extend more, then place a round rod made of cloth or leather on the patient's shoulder, and make it as thick as necessary.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And extend and lift with strength; hold the rod in your hand to ensure the break is evenly set as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the dislocation due to it coming in from the front, then it is fitting that the patient lies over their injured side, and places a middle-sized earring under the shoulder blade, while you, as minister, push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the dislocation rises.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 Then bring the break close to your legs and if you find fragments, cut them below as needed.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 Then lightly grind the pieces and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, use one of your surgical tools.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 But place the scapula with this instrument to support it:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 And appears like a spoon, and is not too sharp, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and strength of the hand:
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 And has two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, like the edges of the wound made when fracturing the bone:
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the edges are small or doubtful about a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloths and bandages according to its quantity:
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes forth, apply oil-soaked cloths and linens soaked in wine, and place on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The breaking of the bone when there are no wounds or indentations, is to put plaster powder from ground mill and goat's milk on it, then place light bandages over it, and set a spindle underne cuff if needed:
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 Then take a very wide band about the width of a palm, then put a double dressing over splints and the frame.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 Then take a slender staff three fingers wide and long, and wrap it entirely with the bandage, ensuring the head of the bandage hangs.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 And place the staff over the fracture, turn the bandage around the neck, and remove it from the good side, and remove it from the injured side.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 And wrap each part separately, and when you see the fracture is aligned properly, and it's clearly evident that the staff does not move over the broken bone, reward it every day, and if the ligaments heal, keep them bound.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 And lay the patient on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder to elevate it.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 If it lightens the fracture of the shoulder by elevating the arm and binding it to the neck, until there is no improper dislocation occurring for twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 Then resume the splint if you see it's needed, and continue to strain and release it until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And it will be restored in at most twenty-eight days, or sooner for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 It often happens that the broken shoulder does not heal properly, and it remains without any strength except by touching.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 If reassembled according to the breakage pattern, and jointed as naturally as possible in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	 Then apply a layer of finely ground powder with plenty of egg whites, and soak it in a double layer.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 Then place a wide and fine bandage over the shoulder, slightly wider than the scapula, ensuring that it is evenly cut at all parts of the shoulder, using flax-linen strips for padding.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	 And then wrap it all with a large and firm bandage, so that the bandage does not move from its place, and inspect each suture daily.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	 And every time it becomes painful, re-bandage and ensure the bandage is still in place properly, and lay the patient on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	 And the shoulder is reset within 20 or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 And when these numbers are completed, if the dislocation occurs again, beware, for it is not bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of bone protrudes without breaking the skin, let it be cauterized as we have mentioned in treating an abscess with hot plasters.
de la brisure dou pis	And for the broken leg.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The flesh is never broken in a thousand, but this happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 but often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken inside, if it moves downwards, the patient feels great pain, weakness, and swelling, and possibly vomits blood, with fractures visible in the bones that are broken, and everything hurts terribly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back, and places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulder blades together with hands, and aligns the rib bones of two ribs in each hand, and skillfully puts them into all possible positions until the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	 then place pads and cotton over the sternum subtly with salt or another light substance, wrap it in one sheet, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	 And turn the ligament into shape at the back, and restrain it momentarily, and reward each hour of freedom, and if it relaxes, then restrain it again.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	 And if it needs to be loosed for corrosion or pruritis that comes on the site, or pain or abscess, act quickly and release it, cleanse the wound, and apply whatever curative methods you know.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then reset the dislocation, and restrain until it is securely in place.
de la brisure des costes	From the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Know that the fractures of the ribs come only in large numbers behind the back and within the head, and they bend solecup because they are brittle.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 And he feels much pain at the touch of the joints.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the healing is such that you align the break as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then place the splint, and use a stiffening rod if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	 And if the fracture of the ribs is descending internally, he feels great pain and swelling, similar to fever, because the bone pierces through.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 and causes pain at the ends, and nausea and vomits large amounts of blood, it is a serious illness, and in ancient times they put great care into treating it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say it should be administered foods that cause the stomach to swell, in order to push the fracture upward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not attempt what we cannot achieve; if there are no puss-filled abscesses present, they will not appear.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have appeared, then apply the treatment.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	 And some say that one puts cups on the area to draw out blood and apply heat therapy, which seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 However, there is also doubt that the cupping does not attract excesses to the area due to its weakening effect.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	; by a.stir ou the set a. ndest; they haved and# s but that t1 this if you. Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	 And if the patient feels such great pain that he cannot bear it from the bone piercing through, and there is doubt for him, then one should cut above where the rib is broken, and use a tool to provide support.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then one must cut the bone, and gently draw it, and then sew the two lips of the wound if they are large, and treat with unguents until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	 And when an abscess occurs, place it under a cloth soaked in oil of roses and apply to the area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat according to what is necessary for an abscess until it is healed properly on the ribs or where they should be.
de la brisure dou col	Of the broken rib fracture
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 Never does a fracture occur in the sternum bone, and rarely that it bends.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 And similarly to the spinal column of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if it will heal or not, be wary if you see his hands becoming softened and swollen and lifeless, unable to move or extend them, and when pricked with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Say that it has fatal outcomes in some cases, and if they move and feel well when constrained and not, know that the bone joint is saved, and the patient will be healed if treated properly.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	 And if a similar thing occurs to the spinal column of the back, and you want to know whether it is healed or not, pay attention if the legs are softened, and if there are accidents that have occurred in hand muscles, and on the back, there is windsweetness and egestion without volition.
