et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	 and similarly those that arise directly in the groin, which cannot be treated except for those properly on the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	 and there are times when the patient's face should be stretched for one even length, and have strain from it so that they do not fidget.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	 then fix a tension in the head on the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a bandage around the limbs of the patient, and one at the calves, and at the knees, and at the ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	 And two ministers know the ligaments, one at the head and the other at the joints, among the two shafts.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 And they should be firmly closed as we have said, and the healer places his palms along the spine, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	 And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a stick three arm lengths long, and sharpen one end, the patient lies on their side, and lift the head of the stick from under the sheet, then place the middle of the stick along the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	 And the healer places his feet on the other end of the stick and presses firmly until it returns to place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if you see this, then do the twist which turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	 And you shall insert two spits on the head of a large arm, one toward each other, and between each spit, there should be an open hand's width of length.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	 And in each prick, provide a covering or bandage, and securely embed the spits in the ground so they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	 And between each pair of spits, there should be another turning prick to which the bands are attached, and in those two pricks, place small pricks one open hand's width long for turning the bandage.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And then tie the band which is among the spikes at the turning point toward the head, and the other band toward the feet at the opposite turning point; each assistant turns their respective turning points throughout the entire bandage, as we have described.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 When they are level, place a dry emplaster with plenty of wax, then the bandages, and then the splint from a tablet of three fingers long, to keep the location of the dislocation and the healthy part of the spine in position, then bind it with a ligature as we have said, and instruct the patient on subtle nourishment until they are well.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	 If no improvement comes at the end of recovery, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medications, with the splint that we have mentioned earlier.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	 And never administer a piece of lead, and never do the appearance come in the rear spine, and believe that it is a dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	 And it is the bone which opens up, hence one must not have any false confidence.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 Perhaps it would bring death upon them.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	 Say that the hip and shoulder joints only come with dislocations, not like other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	 And the hip joint is dislocated in four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	 of anterior and posterior, and front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 and more towards the inner side, while less is dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	 And the knowledge of inner dislocation is that when joining the injured leg with the healthy one, the former is longer and opens more on the unhealthy side than on the healthy, preventing the injured from doubling its angle at the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And it is the body part near a hot abscess swollen, because the hip joint comes close to it.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those who come at disadvantage, so these accidents are contrary to what was mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	 And the signs of those who have this affliction are such that their leg is well-extended as per completion.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 Nevertheless, do not move the knee causing pain, and if one wishes to make it walk, it cannot before, holds its urine, swells with anger, and when it walks, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of those behind are that they cannot expand their knee or double it, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the vein is softened, and the head of the hip to below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	 The reductions of this type of dislocation are that you must reset it as soon as the dislocation occurs, and it remains according to its position, there is no treatment.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 and one should not be overly confident.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	 And in those cases where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways to address it: quickly return the joint, push it back in and secure it, then move it right and left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 In case it returns, no further treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	 And if it does not return in this manner, you must summon a strong healer, and firmly support the leg with two hands or use a bandage placed above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	 And another healer extends his hand over the thigh in a way that places it below the kneecaps and then tightly wraps a light bandage around the hip.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	 And yet another inserts a stick into the bandage.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And they extend both upwards and downwards at once, as long as the patient is raised from the ground at one time, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common in four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is fine.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	 If not, it requires treatment for its resemblance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	 When the dislocation is in the hip, it must be braced with a band around the patient's unaffected side, then place a ligature at the base of the hip, and extend the ligature towards the groin, and upwards towards the abdomen.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	 then use additional supports for its arms, and wrap around the affected hip joint, extending it forward fully:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	 if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	 If you cannot hold it in the manner we have described, then you must tie both of the patient's feet together with a strong but soft band above the two heels and over the two knees, and ensure that the affected leg is extended further than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	 Then it should be hung from a log across its head, and have both arms lengthened apart on the ground.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 Then instruct another minister to cradle the patient's chest, and have other ministers hanging alongside with them who also support the abdomen firmly because the dislocation will now return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	 And when the dislocation is on its way back, lay the patient down as we have mentioned in those with gangrene, and properly loosen the band around the affected leg and over the thigh similarly.
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	 Then apply two heating plasters, one at the head and another elsewhere on the body; then insert a stick between the buttocks near the patient's anus.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And wrap them with wet cloths around, so they do not move the patient; then extend each minister towards him, and ensure he aligns his hand to properly reset the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 But if not, place on a bed or similar, and press as we have said in hernias, and move the patient onto their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	 And when the dislocation is in front, it must be extended with great haste and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 then place the minister's hand on the affected arm, and press with the other hand, extending it towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	 And if the dislocation is behind, do not extend the patient towards the ground or upwards, but rather it must be positioned as though his knees were unlocked at the back, as we have mentioned during supine lying on both heels.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	 And it lies across its face, and the ligament is stretched as we have said before, and you must gently press on the joint to the bone.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	 and it will be pointed when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	 then place the heels together, and put in a splint, and bind with a bandage so that the knee does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	 and rests for three days or four, then unbind it, and put in a splint again;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	 and if you see that they are even, strain as before, and leave for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 then unbind it, and let the patient walk easily until the limb is strong again.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	 The joint is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	 It consists of being dislocated by pushing through internally, externally, and behind.
et ne desalue point devant.	 And it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his thigh, and if it does not reach his thigh, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	 And the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if possible, then place your back to his face, and put your feet under his.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	 Then take its head in your hands, retract it between your thumbs, then bend the two sides of the head shape.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	 And other assistants extend his foot until the joint returns to its place, and the sign is that it slightly feels the leg in its thigh.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	 And apply the poultice on it, and raise the leg to the hip, keeping them together firmly for 3 or 4 days before releasing.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And do not work the patient too much until the limb is comfortably healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not quite straight, it must be strongly extended as we have said in treating knee issues, until it is well aligned.
de la dislocation dou talon	Regarding ankle dislocations
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never fully bent or unbent and within them lie the arteries.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and try to move it towards the part where it has dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 The movements should be light, and when reset, gently extend with hands until fully seated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	 And if it is dislocated completely, then you must make the patient sit straight, and tie him up with ropes outside the leg, above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	 Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand twice, then extend upward firmly and place the foot well above.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	 And do so twice, as we have said, by bending and pulling the foot.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	 If it returns, that is good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	 If not, resume the treatment, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	 And if it cannot return thus, place the patient on their back on the ground and firmly press between their thighs with a passage, and wrap them with cloths around, so they do not shake.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	 Then anoint the minister's thigh and have another minister extend the foot to his hands or the line, so he ties above the neck of the foot.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	 Then extend each minister equally, and the passage be tightly between the patient's thighs to hold when stretching.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 Then position the splints to stabilize the dislocation with your hands, and use other methods to support the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	 And when it reaches a point, apply the bandage and compresses above, make sure to tighten them properly, wrap the cloth around the leg, and protect the nerves behind the ankle so that the bindings are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	 then leave it for two or three days, and if possible loosen the bindings, adjust the straps.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	 then remove on the fourth day or after that, encourage the patient to move around freely for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 and if it progresses before this term is up, do not be concerned that it may still dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, you must calm it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy again.
des dois	:
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be extended without much effort, which is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	 If the dislocation is in any part of the back or foot, it must be made to sit on a flat level or right-angled table, and place your foot under which of these joints are separated, then press firmly with your foot until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	 And when it is level and nothing is apart, place under the sole of your foot a two-legged table, then strain firmly, and let it be for three days, then release.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And make it rest until it is sound.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	 When wound comes with the dislocation and we see its restoration, many times it happens that patients die:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	 If you are not presumptuous in the treatment, unless you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compasserate and slow to act, do not be hasty.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	 At the beginning of healing, apply to an abscess until it is drained, and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope for health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And when you see hope, now reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess may properly heal.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	 And when the limb is back in place, apply soothing remedies to the abscess and treat the wound as it should be, with drying ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	 And if there is also a bone break and small pieces to be removed, follow what we have said in simple illnesses.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 And be wary of falling into despair, as I have said, for it will affect your health according to your Maker, and for the safety of your weapon and body.
